<username>Alejandro Martinez< /username><date>1327469790846<//date><Rating>4</Rating>< text>
The pizza is good, although I personally believe there is better pizza out there, if you are willing to pay 30% more. But for the price, you get a great value. It's also a fun place to go. People are very friendly. If you go on a date, try the pasta dishes, and some good wine. An excellent way to spend a Friday or Saturdy evening is to go to the movies next door, then come over for a nice dinner. I also go there from time to time, and just hang out by the bar and have a drink. Usually, there are some people hanging out, and you can enjoy a relaxed evening.< /text>

< text>
Living in the Bay Area, I needed a birthday gift for my son's girlfriend who lives in Truckee.  I wanted to support a local shop during the Covid 19 shut down so my son suggested Bespoke.  Heather was fantastic and very patient as she sent me photos of products that were not all posted on the website.  Once I choose the item, she set it out for curb side pick up.  My son said it was beautifully wrapped and Heather even filled out the card with  my personal message.  I encourage anyone needing a gift to reach out to Bespoke. <name>Stephen Cook<//name>< time>
1614022517354<//time>
<Rate>5</Rate>< review>
This place had great authentic food and wasn't too crowded on a Saturday night. We made reservations and they were really accommodating for 12 people.

The tea leaf salad is a must, it's mainly nuts and it's really savory. It's something really unique you should try if you've never had it before. They had a variety of spicy levels but we got non-spicy since some people in our party are not a big fan of spicy food. The food was really great even though it didn't have heat to it! The roti was great, really thick yet soft and the dipping sauce it came with had great flavor.

The samosas were probably one of my favorite dishes, really flavorful and crunchy! We ordered several chicken and beef dishes as well as a few noodle dishes. I was impressed with each one that I tried and would definitely recommend this place to people in the area. I've tried several great Burmese places in SF and I would definitely count this restaurant as a favorite.<//review>

< Review>
Burma Love and Burma Superstar get all the glory in SF, and to be sure, they are very good. But Mandalay Restaurant is my Burmese bae. Everything I've had here at the city's oldest Burmese restaurant has just been so incredibly, aggressively flavorful (but in the best way possible) and delicious. My top choices are the spicy smoked pork with cabbages, the prawns with green beans, the papaya salad, the fried squash sticks, and the Mandalay special noodles. The prices are also super reasonable. It's one of my favorite restaurants in a pretty stacked Inner Richmond scene.<//Review>

<username>Samantha Berg</username><date>1497387548121< /date><rate>3<//rate>< Review>
Just not as good as Burma Superstar.

I love the idea of finding a Burmese place that's as tasty as Burma Superstar with less of the wait, but I just haven't been able to do it. This one is good, it's just not that same level.

Highlights: balada (esp the curry dipping sauce), rainbow salad, rangoon lamb (so tender!)

The staff is friendly and I'd probably come back if I was in the area, but not when I'm hitting a real craving.<//Review>

A Burmese restaurant tucked away, didn't try a lot of different dishes, the tea leaf salad surprised me as there was no other greens! Not sure if this is more authentic, but I'm more used to the Burma Superstar tea leaf salad. The final presentation after it was mixed up, definitely was not the most appetizing. The crispy chicken was truly unique and the presentation was artistic. The coconut rice was with coconut flavor which I thought was well done! And on each table, there's a dish of spice!<//Text>

< Rating>
4</Rating>
< Review>
Really enjoyed the food. This place is apparently the original Burmese restaurant in SF. A lot of the decor felt authentic and we enjoyed the overall feel. The service was awkward and forced. They kept asking if I was ready to order about every minute to 45 seconds. Felt a little pushy to get some other stuff on the menu too. We had the chicken curry and their noodle dish. The curry was succulent and the noodle dish was even better than the sister store of the famous Burmese Star imo. Amazing mix of textures and flavors. Notes of bay leaf wafted and was almost freshly aromatic as your chewing, but the coconut chicken with noodles felt like comfort food. If you like Thai, Indian, or Burmese, this is a must try in SF. Would give a 3.7 if I could, or a 4.5 if the service wasn‚Äôt so awkward.</Review>

<Rating>5</Rating><Text>This Burmese restaurant has one of the best Tea Leaf salads in the city. I recently discovered this place post COVID and I am impressed by the food and also the staff. The restaurant is currently offering outdoor seating and the staff tries very hard to give you a great dining experience. When I went to eat at this restaurant, it was very cold and windy outside. The staff brought out portable heating lamps and even a dividing wall to protect our table from the wind. They kept checking in on us to ensure that we were comfortable. Overall their customer service was great.

Now on to the food, I've tried their tea leaf salad, rainbow chicken, garlic noodles and mango sticky rice.  Every plate was delicious and the portions are perfect for two people. I believe this restaurant was even Michelin rated a few years back. I am glad that I discovered this place but I wish I had found it sooner!<//Text><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< Response>

<user_name>Stephen Collins< /user_name><date>1520785382270</date>< Text>
Some of the best service I've ever seen in a restaurant. Attentive, friendly, helpful, creative, aware, and very quick - these folks really have it dialed in. Our wait staff understood all aspects of pescatarian, vegetarian, and vegan at our table, and was very clear and helpful as to each specific dish and what modifications could be made.

Food: anywhere from pretty good to excellent, depending on the dish - with bonus points for novelty since I rarely eat Burmese. It seems they fry their own tofu which makes a world of difference.

Decor: dated but authentic. Someone taking care of the Orchids up front really knows what they're doing.< /Text>

<review>I absolutely adore this place. Two of my favorite dishes: glazed deep-fried eggplant and volcano beef. The beef is not on the menu, but they have never turned me away when I've ordered it. It's a slightly spicy, slightly sweet, touch of cumin maybe?, incredibly tender beef with peppers and onions. The eggplant is cut into huge chunks with a sugar-crisp fried outer and moist, almost airy center. Also a touch spicy. Those are just the entrees. Two other favorites are the balada and samusa salad. The balada is basically a paratha, an light, flaky flat bread served with a gingery curry sauce. I like to smear a few spoonfuls of the chili paste, top it with curry sauce, and fold it like a pizza to eat. The samusa salad is a lovely mix of textures and flavors. You get crispy samusa and batter-fried veggies mixed with fresh veggies, dressed in a slightly sour, slightly sweet tamarind dressing. I could easily just eat balada and samusa salad for dinner (split with someone else because the portions are generous). Add this to your dining bucket list.</review>< Pictures>

<Rate>5</Rate><Review>My favorite Burmese restaurant in the city: the waits are not as crazy as the other places and the food has always been deliciously dependable.

My favorite (and therefore always ordered) items:
1.  Rainbow Salad: there are twenty ingredients in this thing, and together they make a divine dish.  I could eat this for a meal alone if it were just me.
2.  Mandalay Special Noodle:  normally I'm not a huge coconut fan, but it works in this dish.  The cooked noodles and the crunchy noodles complement each other in texture, and the chicken is always tender and nicely flavored.
3.  Mango chicken:  the sauce on the chicken is so delicious.  The mango chunks aren't always the sweetest, but that's not always a bad thing given it's a savory dish.
4.  Dry pan-fried string beans with tofu: just get them.  Seriously.
5.  Also have tried the tea leaf salad, which is also good, but I still prefer the rainbow salad.  Will order if I want to change it up.

True, the portions do leave something to be desired, but I suppose it prevents me from eating too much to the point of bursting.</Review><pictures>None< /pictures><Resp>None</Resp><Gmap_id>0x8085873c9a913065:0x788e4b120aaaa7d5</Gmap_id></record>

<userid>103224758490004547191<//userid><username>Thomas Martin< /username><time>1574787528004<//time><rating>3</rating><text>Cozy little Burmese restaurant in the Inner Richmond on California Street in an area where parking can be challenging. Colorfully decorated and illuminated with a table of fruit offerings to a small Buddha near the entrance and small booths in the center and tables along the sides. We sat in a booth and were greeted almost immediately by a very friendly, Chinese waitress. The somewhat kitchy ambiance and attentive service were the high points of the evening.
We were looking forward to ordering a Tea Leaf Salad, but both the picture and the description looked far too "nutty" for our tastes. The online menu listed an Indian Naan bread, but it is not available, so we ordered a Balada (Burmese pancake) which we all enjoyed despite the non-descript sauce/gravy that accompanied it.
I was curious to try a Burmese curry and ordered a shrimp curry, only to discover that it really wasn't a curry at all. It came with a bland tomato and onion sauce, in no way similar to an Indian, Thai, or Chinese curry.  Our waitress informed me that that the chicken or beef curry was a more traditional, spicy curry, but curry lovers should take warning. One of my Chinese friends who had recent dental work ordered a plate of noodles which seemed either too soft or overcooked, which in this case may have been fortunate. My other Chinese friend ordered the Szechuan Beef which was clearly the best tasting dish on the table, although it was not very spicy even though it featured lots of green and red peppers.
I confess we had come to Mandala because we wanted to eat Burmese food at Pagan Restaurant on Clement and 33rd, but it was closed. Frankly  while the interior of Mandalay was far more inviting than Pagan, the food was disappointing. It was also far less Burmese. Pagan appears to be something of a family run Burmese operation with Burmese and Thai food, while Manadaly appears to be a Burmese restaurant with Burmese and Chinese food with a largel;y Chinese staff.</text>< Pictures>
None<//Pictures>

< Text>
The hidden Burmese food gem of San Francisco. Don't be fooled by the hype.
There's nothing wrong with Burma Superstar, except the endless lines and tiny dining room.
Mandalay is more than twice the size, and just as good.
My personal favorite is the 'birds nest seafood delight' which is a seafood and vegetable stir fry served in a crispy, edible bowl, but everything I've tried there has been good, especially the tea leaf salad!
This is also a great place to take vegetarians, as there's a wide variety of options available for them.
They also offer both chopsticks and forks automatically, in case you're not comfortable with chopsticks.
There's also several interesting and tasty drink options (as well as the classic young coconut) and a wine menu.

Go two blocks off Clement, away from the crazy wait times, and get food that's far better in my mind.<//Text>

< review>
I have to dock a couple of stars from my last review.

They placed my party at this table which was awkwardly placed next to another (imagine two square tables and one of them rotated into a diamond).  I know they're pressed for space, but this was ridiculous.

I noticed that the prices went up, which isn't a surprise living here in the city.  I ordered the sizzling rice soup, which by all accounts was delicious and satisfied my craving for something warm.  My roommate ordered lamb, but was given chicken.  It took awhile to flag a waiter down to correct the order.  My other roommate wanted more vegetables in her dish and was told to order a side of vegetables instead.  Plus she was told it was pre-made, which makes me wonder how much of their food is just waiting under heat lamps...

I hope the owners/management get together soon because it would be a shame if they closed.  The food is really good, especially the string beans.  But if service continues this way, and prices go up, no one is going to line up to eat here.  And I say that because that is usually the norm.  I was surprised we got a table right away, and surprised there weren't groups of people waiting after we left.<//review>

< Review>
Mandalay has been open 26 years, and I've been eating there for 25. In my experience, it's the best Burmese restaurant in the City, with a mix of Burmese specialties and Chinese dishes. I eat only the Burmese, which can be thought of as a flavor mix of Thai, Indian, and Chinese with a special twist of its own. I especially recommend the Ginger Salad and Tampoi Rice. Weekends can be noisy.</Review>

The Vibe: Burmese cuisine that many people can get down with

Special Dish: Tea Salad, Fish Soup, Special Noodles

Avoid Their: n/a

Price Point: most big entrees are under $20.00 while small dishes are under $7.00

< Text>
We have been coming here for years & did not realize that we had not reviewed this. Mandalay is one of our favorite restaurants in the world. We always get great food & personalized warm service. I would mention that it gets busy, as we found this holiday season, so call them for reservations. They are not on Open Table anymore. The vegetarian & vegan  options are incredible. We love the had balada, samusa soup, tea leaf salad, ginger salad, walnut broccoli tofu, Mandalay special noodle, & coconut rice. The tofu kebat, Singapore noodles, & basil spicy eggplant are okay. The desserts & drinks are also great. Parking can be tough in the area.< /Text>

<review>I've passed by Mandalay a few times, without realizing they're the sister restaurant to Mingalaba, which is easily my favorite Burmese restaurant in the Bay Area. On the suggestion of a friend, her boyfriend and I came here instead of Burma Superstar, and ordered the:

* Tea Leaf Salad - What Burmese meal is complete without one of these! As flavorful as the ones at Mingalaba, but a bit saltier, with some minor flavor differences, and also possibly smaller.

* Mandalay Special Noodles - I'm not sure if these are the same as the house noodles at Mingalaba, but quite similar in any case, and just as delicious.

* Mango Prawns - This was a bit of an odd order, but we wanted to diversify our protein a bit, and opted for seafood. Not a bad dish, but not exactly what I imagined (which was something more saucy), and a bit on the salty side, even when paired with rice.

So, be it due to poor memory, or actual difference in quality of the food, Mandalay wasn't as impressive as Mingalaba, but still good enough that it beats out having to wait in line at Burma Superstar.

***Accessibility Info***

Venue - The restaurant is quite a large space, so getting around isn't a problem.

Bathroom - Didn't check them out.</review><pics>None< /pics>< Resp>
None<//Resp>

<review>Wow! This rivals Burma IMHO. It was fairly crowded on a Thursday evening but we got a table within 15 min. The seafood rangoon is a must, as well as the braised pork served in whole kabocha squash (which made quite a lovely presentation). The seafood was tender and the sauce was tangy and flavorful. < Text>
Most people know about Burma Superstar one block away, but this little hidden treasure is my favorite. The way Mandalay prepares the quintessential Burmese dish Laphet (tealeaf salad) is much more authentic than Burma Superstar. (I should know--I grew up in Rangoon, Burma.) At Mandalay, you get a generous dose of fermented tealeaf, with little or no green. That's the way it ought to be. My other favorite items on the menu are stir-fried sour leaves (Chinbaung), mango chicken, and Nan gyi thoke.</Text>
